database_connector.py
```python
'''
DatabaseConnector class for connecting to PostgreSQL database.
'''
import psycopg2
class DatabaseConnector:
    def __init__(self, db_params):
        self.db_params = db_params
        self.connection = None
    def connect(self):
        self.connection = psycopg2.connect(**self.db_params)
    def fetch_data(self, query):
        with self.connection.cursor() as cursor:
            cursor.execute(query)
            return cursor.fetchall()
```
data_ingestor.py
```python
'''
DataIngestor class for ingesting CSV data into the database.
'''
import pandas as pd
from sqlalchemy import create_engine
class DataIngestor:
    def __init__(self, db_connector):
        self.db_connector = db_connector
    def ingest_csv(self, file_path):
        try:
            # Read CSV file
            data = pd.read_csv(file_path)
            # Create SQLAlchemy engine for table creation
            engine = create_engine(f'postgresql://{self.db_connector.db_params["user"]}:{self.db_connector.db_params["password"]}@{self.db_connector.db_params["host"]}/{self.db_connector.db_params["dbname"]}')
            # Check if table exists and create if not
            data.to_sql('shop_floor_data', engine, if_exists='replace', index=False)  # Use 'replace' for initial load
        except FileNotFoundError:
            print(f"Error: The file {file_path} was not found.")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
```
data_analyzer.py
```python
'''
DataAnalyzer class for analyzing shop-floor data.
'''
import pandas as pd
class DataAnalyzer:
    def __init__(self, db_connector):
        self.db_connector = db_connector
    def analyze_data(self):
        query = "SELECT * FROM shop_floor_data"
        data = self.db_connector.fetch_data(query)
        # Analyze data for efficiency issues
        efficiency_issues = []
        # Convert fetched data to DataFrame for easier analysis
        df = pd.DataFrame(data, columns=['event_time', 'equipment_id', 'status', 'duration', 'output'])
        # Define thresholds for analysis
        threshold_duration = 10  # Example threshold for long durations
        threshold_output = 5      # Example threshold for low output
        # Identify bottlenecks (e.g., long durations)
        long_durations = df[df['duration'] > threshold_duration]
        if not long_durations.empty:
            efficiency_issues.append(f"Bottlenecks identified in {len(long_durations)} events with long durations.")
        # Identify efficiency gaps (e.g., low output)
        low_output = df[df['output'] < threshold_output]
        if not low_output.empty:
            efficiency_issues.append(f"Efficiency gaps identified in {len(low_output)} events with low output.")
        # Add more analysis as needed...
        return efficiency_issues
```
report_generator.py
```python
'''
ReportGenerator class for generating Jupyter notebook reports.
'''
import nbformat as nbf
class ReportGenerator:
    def __init__(self, analysis_results):
        self.analysis_results = analysis_results
    def generate_report(self, output_path):
        nb = nbf.v4.new_notebook()
        nb.cells.append(nbf.v4.new_markdown_cell("# Efficiency Report"))
        for issue in self.analysis_results:
            nb.cells.append(nbf.v4.new_markdown_cell(f"## {issue}"))
        with open(output_path, 'w') as f:
            nbf.write(nb, f)
```
gui.py
```python
'''
GUI class for the application.
'''
from tkinter import Frame, Button, Label, filedialog
from database_connector import DatabaseConnector
from data_ingestor import DataIngestor
from data_analyzer import DataAnalyzer
from report_generator import ReportGenerator
class App:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        master.title("Shop Floor Efficiency Analyzer")
        self.label = Label(master, text="Shop Floor Efficiency Analyzer")
        self.label.pack()
        self.ingest_button = Button(master, text="Ingest CSV", command=self.ingest_csv)
        self.ingest_button.pack()
        self.analyze_button = Button(master, text="Analyze Data", command=self.analyze_data)
        self.analyze_button.pack()
        self.report_button = Button(master, text="Generate Report", command=self.generate_report)
        self.report_button.pack()
        self.db_connector = DatabaseConnector({"dbname": "your_db", "user": "your_user", "password": "your_password", "host": "localhost"})
        self.db_connector.connect()
    def ingest_csv(self):
        file_path = filedialog.askopenfilename()
        ingestor = DataIngestor(self.db_connector)
        ingestor.ingest_csv(file_path)
    def analyze_data(self):
        analyzer = DataAnalyzer(self.db_connector)
        self.analysis_results = analyzer.analyze_data()
    def generate_report(self):
        report_generator = ReportGenerator(self.analysis_results)
        report_generator.generate_report("efficiency_report.ipynb")
```

database_connector.py
```python
'''
DatabaseConnector class for connecting to PostgreSQL database.
'''
import psycopg2
class DatabaseConnector:
    def __init__(self, db_params):
        self.db_params = db_params
        self.connection = None
    def connect(self):
        self.connection = psycopg2.connect(**self.db_params)
    def fetch_data(self, query):
        with self.connection.cursor() as cursor:
            cursor.execute(query)
            return cursor.fetchall()
```

data_ingestor.py
```python
'''
DataIngestor class for ingesting CSV data into the database.
'''
import pandas as pd
from sqlalchemy import create_engine
class DataIngestor:
    def __init__(self, db_connector):
        self.db_connector = db_connector
    def ingest_csv(self, file_path):
        try:
            # Read CSV file
            data = pd.read_csv(file_path)
            # Create SQLAlchemy engine for table creation
            engine = create_engine(f'postgresql://{self.db_connector.db_params["user"]}:{self.db_connector.db_params["password"]}@{self.db_connector.db_params["host"]}/{self.db_connector.db_params["dbname"]}')
            # Check if table exists and create if not
            data.to_sql('shop_floor_data', engine, if_exists='replace', index=False)  # Use 'replace' for initial load
        except FileNotFoundError:
            print(f"Error: The file {file_path} was not found.")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
```

data_analyzer.py
```python
'''
DataAnalyzer class for analyzing shop-floor data.
'''
import pandas as pd
class DataAnalyzer:
    def __init__(self, db_connector):
        self.db_connector = db_connector
    def analyze_data(self):
        query = "SELECT * FROM shop_floor_data"
        data = self.db_connector.fetch_data(query)
        # Analyze data for efficiency issues
        efficiency_issues = []
        # Convert fetched data to DataFrame for easier analysis
        df = pd.DataFrame(data, columns=['event_time', 'equipment_id', 'status', 'duration', 'output'])
        # Define thresholds for analysis
        threshold_duration = 10  # Example threshold for long durations
        threshold_output = 5      # Example threshold for low output
        # Identify bottlenecks (e.g., long durations)
        long_durations = df[df['duration'] > threshold_duration]
        if not long_durations.empty:
            efficiency_issues.append(f"Bottlenecks identified in {len(long_durations)} events with long durations.")
        # Identify efficiency gaps (e.g., low output)
        low_output = df[df['output'] < threshold_output]
        if not low_output.empty:
            efficiency_issues.append(f"Efficiency gaps identified in {len(low_output)} events with low output.")
        # Add more analysis as needed...
        return efficiency_issues
```

report_generator.py
```python
'''
ReportGenerator class for generating Jupyter notebook reports.
'''
import nbformat as nbf
class ReportGenerator:
    def __init__(self, analysis_results):
        self.analysis_results = analysis_results
    def generate_report(self, output_path):
        nb = nbf.v4.new_notebook()
        nb.cells.append(nbf.v4.new_markdown_cell("# Efficiency Report"))
        for issue in self.analysis_results:
            nb.cells.append(nbf.v4.new_markdown_cell(f"## {issue}"))
        with open(output_path, 'w') as f:
            nbf.write(nb, f)
```

gui.py
```python
'''
GUI class for the application.
'''
from tkinter import Frame, Button, Label, filedialog
from database_connector import DatabaseConnector
from data_ingestor import DataIngestor
from data_analyzer import DataAnalyzer
from report_generator import ReportGenerator
class App:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        master.title("Shop Floor Efficiency Analyzer")
        self.label = Label(master, text="Shop Floor Efficiency Analyzer")
        self.label.pack()
        self.ingest_button = Button(master, text="Ingest CSV", command=self.ingest_csv)
        self.ingest_button.pack()
        self.analyze_button = Button(master, text="Analyze Data", command=self.analyze_data)
        self.analyze_button.pack()
        self.report_button = Button(master, text="Generate Report", command=self.generate_report)
        self.report_button.pack()
        self.db_connector = DatabaseConnector({"dbname": "your_db", "user": "your_user", "password": "your_password", "host": "localhost"})
        self.db_connector.connect()
    def ingest_csv(self):
        file_path = filedialog.askopenfilename()
        ingestor = DataIngestor(self.db_connector)
        ingestor.ingest_csv(file_path)
    def analyze_data(self):
        analyzer = DataAnalyzer(self.db_connector)
        self.analysis_results = analyzer.analyze_data()
    def generate_report(self):
        report_generator = ReportGenerator(self.analysis_results)
        report_generator.generate_report("efficiency_report.ipynb")
```

Building applications with LLMs through composability

## 🤔 What is this?

Large language models (LLMs) are emerging as a transformative technology, enabling developers to build applications that they previously could not. However, using these LLMs in isolation is often insufficient for creating a truly powerful app - the real power comes when you can combine them with other sources of computation or knowledge.

This library aims to assist in the development of those types of applications. Common examples of these applications include:

```markdown
# Shop Floor Efficiency Analyzer

The Shop Floor Efficiency Analyzer is a Python application designed to connect to a PostgreSQL database, ingest shop-floor event data and equipment metrics from CSV files, analyze the data for bottlenecks and efficiency gaps, and generate a report in the form of a Jupyter notebook. This tool aims to help organizations identify inefficiencies in their operations and suggest potential savings.

## Main Functions

1. **Database Connection**: Connects to a PostgreSQL database to fetch and store shop-floor data.
2. **CSV Ingestion**: Allows users to upload CSV files containing shop-floor event data for analysis.
3. **Data Analysis**: Analyzes the ingested data to identify efficiency issues and bottlenecks.
4. **Report Generation**: Outputs a Jupyter notebook containing a report of identified efficiency issues and potential savings.

## Installation

To set up the environment and install the necessary dependencies, follow these steps:

1. **Clone the Repository**:
   ```bash
   git clone https://github.com/your-repo/shop-floor-efficiency-analyzer.git
   cd shop-floor-efficiency-analyzer
   ```

2. **Create a Virtual Environment** (optional but recommended):
   ```bash
   python -m venv venv
   source venv/bin/activate  # On Windows use `venv\Scripts\activate`
   ```

3. **Install Required Packages**:
   Make sure you have `pip` installed, then run:
   ```bash
   pip install psycopg2 pandas sqlalchemy nbformat
   ```

4. **Install Tkinter** (if not already installed):
   Tkinter is usually included with Python installations. If you encounter issues, you may need to install it separately depending on your OS.

## Usage

1. **Run the Application**:
   Start the application by executing the main script:
   ```bash
   python main.py
   ```

2. **Ingest CSV Data**:
   - Click the "Ingest CSV" button in the GUI.
   - A file dialog will open; select the CSV file you wish to upload.
   - The data will be ingested into the PostgreSQL database.

3. **Analyze Data**:
   - Click the "Analyze Data" button to perform the analysis on the ingested data.
   - The application will identify efficiency issues and store the results for reporting.

4. **Generate Report**:
   - Click the "Generate Report" button to create a Jupyter notebook report.
   - The report will be saved as `efficiency_report.ipynb` in the current directory.

## Example CSV Format

Ensure your CSV files are formatted correctly. An example structure is as follows:

```csv
event_time,equipment_id,status,duration,output
2023-01-01 08:00:00,EQ1,Running,12,4
2023-01-01 08:05:00,EQ2,Idle,5,6
2023-01-01 08:10:00,EQ1,Running,15,3
```

## Conclusion

The Shop Floor Efficiency Analyzer is a powerful tool for organizations looking to optimize their operations. By following the steps outlined in this manual, users can easily set up the application, ingest data, analyze it, and generate insightful reports to drive efficiency improvements.

For further assistance, please contact support at support@yourcompany.com.
```
